2:25:1495:0:14:72:536:700:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Sensitivity to Missing Data Assumptions: Theory and An Evaluation of the U.S. Wage Structure
2:26:1587:14:14:72:229:686:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Patrick Kline and Andres Santos
2:27:1618:14:14:72:234:672:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:NBER Working Paper No. 15716
2:28:1646:14:14:72:260:658:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:February 2010, Revised February 2011
2:29:1682:14:28:72:166:644:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:JEL No. C01,C1,J3
2:30:1699:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:31:1707:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:This paper develops methods for assessing the sensitivity of empirical conclusions regarding conditional
2:32:1811:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:distributions to departures from the missing at random (MAR) assumption. We index the degree of
2:33:1906:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:non-ignorable selection governing the missingness process by the maximal Kolmogorov-Smirnov
2:34:1997:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:(KS) distance between the distributions of missing and observed outcomes across all values of the
2:35:2094:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:covariates. Sharp bounds on minimum mean square approximations to conditional quantiles are derived
2:36:2193:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:as a function of the nominal level of selection considered in the sensitivity analysis and a weighted
2:37:2294:14:14:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:bootstrap procedure is developed for conducting inference. Using these techniques, we conduct an
2:38:2390:14:14:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:empirical assessment of the sensitivity of observed earnings patterns in U.S. Census data to deviations
2:39:2493:14:14:72:540:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:from the MAR assumption. We find that the well-documented increase in the returns to schooling
2:40:2587:14:14:72:540:462:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:between 1980 and 1990 is relatively robust to deviations from the missing at random assumption except
2:41:2688:14:14:72:540:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:at the lowest quantiles of the distribution, but that conclusions regarding heterogeneity in returns and
2:42:2792:14:42:72:540:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:changes in the returns function between 1990 and 2000 are very sensitive to departures from ignorability.
2:43:2897:42:14:72:136:392:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Patrick Kline
2:44:2910:14:14:72:198:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Department of Economics
2:45:2933:14:14:72:138:364:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:UC, Berkeley
2:46:2945:14:14:72:189:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:508-1 Evans Hall #3880
2:47:2967:14:14:72:171:336:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Berkeley, CA 94720
2:48:2985:14:14:72:124:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:and NBER
2:49:2993:14:28:72:200:308:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:pkline@econ.berkeley.edu
2:50:3017:28:14:72:142:280:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Andres Santos
2:51:3030:14:14:72:198:266:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Department of Economics
2:52:3053:14:14:72:165:252:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:9500 Gilman Drive
2:53:3070:14:14:72:194:238:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:La Jolla, CA 92093-0508
2:54:3093:14:124:72:167:224:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:a2santos@ucsd.edu
2:55:3110:124:14:72:239:100:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:An online appendix is available at:
2:56:3145:14:0:72:283:86:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:http://www.nber.org/data-appendix/w15716
3:57:3185:0:38:43:179:771:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:1  Introduction
3:58:3200:38:17:43:547:733:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Despite major advances in the design and collection of survey and administrative data, missingness
3:59:3298:17:18:43:547:716:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:remains a pervasive feature of virtually every modern economic dataset.  Hirsch and Schumacher
3:60:3392:18:18:43:547:698:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2004),  for instance,  find that nearly 30% of the earnings observations in the Outgoing Rotation
3:61:3490:18:18:43:547:680:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Groups of the Current Population Survey are imputed.  Similar allocation rates are present in other
3:62:3589:18:18:43:547:662:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:major earnings sources such as the March CPS and Decennial Census with the problem growing
3:63:3679:18:26:43:182:644:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worse in more recent years.
3:64:3706:26:18:60:546:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The dominant framework for dealing with missing data has been to assume that it is “missing
3:65:3797:18:18:43:547:600:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at random” (Rubin (1976)) or “ignorable” conditional on observable demographics; an assumption
3:66:3891:18:18:43:547:582:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whose popularity owes more to convenience than plausibility.  Even in settings where it is reason-
3:67:3989:18:18:43:547:564:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:able to believe that non-response is approximately ignorable, the extent of missingness in modern
3:68:4086:18:17:43:547:546:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economic data suggests that economists ought to assess the sensitivity of their conclusions to small
3:69:4186:17:26:43:210:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deviations from this assumption.
3:70:4218:26:18:60:546:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Previous work on non-ignorable missing data processes has either relied upon parametric models
3:71:4312:18:18:43:547:485:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of missingness in conjunction with exclusion restrictions to obtain point identification (Greenlees
3:72:4411:18:18:43:547:467:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (1982) and Lillard et al. (1986)) or considered the “worst case” bounds on population moments
3:73:4511:18:18:43:547:449:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that result when all assumptions regarding the missingness process are abandoned (Manski (1994,
3:74:4606:18:18:43:547:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2003)).   Neither  approach  has  garnered  much  popularity.1It  is  typically  quite  difficult  to  find
3:75:4713:18:18:43:547:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variables which shift the probability of missingness but are uncorrelated with population outcomes.
3:76:4812:18:18:43:547:395:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:And for  most applied problems,  the  worst case bounds  are overly  conservative in  the  sense that
3:77:4913:18:25:43:436:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they consider missingness processes unlikely to be found in modern datasets.
3:78:4989:25:18:60:546:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We propose here an alternative approach for use in settings where one lacks prior knowledge of
3:79:5083:18:18:43:547:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the missing data mechanism.  Rather than ask what can be learned about the parameters of interest
3:80:5180:18:18:43:547:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:given assumptions on the missingness process,  we investigate the level of non-ignorable selection
3:81:5278:18:18:43:547:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:necessary to undermine ones’ conclusions regarding the conditional distribution of the data obtained
3:82:5378:18:18:43:547:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:under  a  missing  at  random  (MAR)  assumption.   We  do  so  by  making  use  of  a  nonparametric
3:83:5479:18:18:43:547:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measure of selection – the maximal Kolmogorov-Smirnov (KS) distance between the distributions
3:84:5572:18:18:43:547:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  missing  and  observed  outcomes  across  all  values  of  the  covariates.   The  KS  distance  yields  a
3:85:5682:18:18:43:547:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:natural parameterization of deviations from ignorability, with a distance of zero corresponding to
3:86:5780:18:18:43:547:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:MAR and a distance of one encompassing the totally unrestricted missingness processes considered
3:87:5876:18:17:43:547:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in Manski (1994).  Between these extremes lie a continuum of selection mechanisms which may be
3:88:5970:17:18:43:547:173:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:studied to determine a critical level of selection above which conclusions obtained under an analysis
3:89:6071:18:26:43:261:155:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:predicated upon MAR may be overturned.
3:90:6109:26:18:60:546:129:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To  enable  such  an  analysis,  we  begin  by  deriving  sharp  bounds  on  the  conditional  quantile
3:91:6212:18:18:43:547:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function  (CQF)  under  nominal  restrictions  on  the  degree  of  selection  present.   We  focus  on  the
3:92:6320:18:18:43:547:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:commonly encountered setting where outcome data are missing and covariates are discrete.  In order
3:93:6418:18:0:56:423:75:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:A:1See DiNardo et al. (2006) for an applied example comparing these two approaches.
4:94:6500:0:18:43:547:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to facilitate the analysis of datasets with many covariates, results are also developed summarizing the
4:95:6603:18:18:43:547:753:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conclusions that can be drawn regarding “pseudo-true” parametric approximations to the underlying
4:96:6700:18:18:43:547:735:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonparametric CQF of the sort considered by Chamberlain (1994).  When point identification of the
4:97:6797:18:18:43:547:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:CQF fails due to missingness, the identified set of pseudo true parameters consists of all coefficients
4:98:6900:18:25:43:547:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:associated with minimum mean square approximations to functions lying within the CQF bounds.
4:99:6992:25:18:60:546:674:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We obtain sharp bounds on the coordinates of the pseudo true parameter vector and propose
4:100:7081:18:18:43:547:656:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:computationally simple estimators for them.  We show that these estimators converge in distribution
4:101:7180:18:18:43:547:638:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to a Gaussian process indexed by the quantile of interest and the level of the nominal restriction on
4:102:7281:18:18:43:547:620:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:selection and develop a weighted bootstrap procedure for consistently estimating that distribution.
4:103:7380:18:18:43:547:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This procedure enables inference on the entire pseudo-true quantile process as indexed both by the
4:104:7478:18:26:43:329:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quantile of interest and the level of the selection bound.
4:105:7536:26:18:60:546:558:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Substantively  these  methods  allow  a  determination  of  the  critical  level  of  selection  for  which
4:106:7643:18:18:43:547:540:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hypotheses regarding conditional quantiles, parametric approximations to conditional quantiles, or
4:107:7741:18:17:43:547:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entire conditional distributions cannot be rejected.  For example we study the “breakdown” function
4:108:7840:17:18:43:547:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:defined implicitly as the level of selection necessary for conclusions to be overturned at each quantile.
4:109:7945:18:18:43:547:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The uniform confidence region for this function effectively summarizes the differential sensitivity of
4:110:8047:18:18:43:547:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the entire conditional distribution to violations of MAR. These techniques substantially extend the
4:111:8146:18:18:43:547:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recent econometrics literature on sensitivity analysis (Altonji et al. (2005, 2008),  Imbens (2003),
4:112:8246:18:18:43:547:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Rosenbaum and Rubin (1983), Rosenbaum (2002)), most of which has focused on the sensitivity of
4:113:8340:18:18:43:547:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:scalar treatment effect estimates to confounding influences, typically by using assumed parametric
4:114:8438:18:26:43:143:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models of selection.
4:115:8458:26:18:60:546:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Having established our inferential procedures, we turn to an empirical assessment of the sensi-
4:116:8553:18:18:43:547:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tivity of heavily studied patterns in the conditional distribution of U.S. wages to deviations from
4:117:8652:18:17:43:547:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the MAR assumption.  We begin by revisiting the results of Angrist et al. (2006) regarding changes
4:118:8750:17:18:43:547:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:across Decennial Censuses in the quantile specific returns to schooling.  Weekly earnings informa-
4:119:8848:18:18:43:547:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion is missing for roughly a quarter of the observations in their study, suggesting the results may
4:120:8948:18:18:43:547:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be sensitive to small deviations from ignorability.  We show that despite extensive missingness in
4:121:9046:18:18:43:547:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the dependent variable, the well-documented increase in the returns to schooling between 1980 and
4:122:9143:18:18:43:547:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1990 is relatively robust to deviations from the missing at random assumption except at the lowest
4:123:9241:18:18:43:547:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quantiles of the conditional distribution.  However, deterioration in the quality of Decennial Census
4:124:9342:18:18:43:547:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:data renders conclusions regarding heterogeneity in returns and changes in the returns function be-
4:125:9441:18:18:43:547:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tween 1990 and 2000 very sensitive to departures from ignorability at all quantiles.  We also show,
4:126:9540:18:18:43:547:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using a more flexible model studied by Lemieux (2006),  that the apparent convexification of the
4:127:9636:18:18:43:547:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:earnings-education profile between 1980 and 2000 is robust to modest deviations from MAR while
4:128:9730:18:25:43:487:138:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:changes in the wage structure at lower quantiles are more easily obscured by selection.
4:129:9817:25:18:60:546:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To gauge the practical relevance of these sensitivity results we analyze a sample of workers from
4:130:9914:18:18:43:547:95:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the 1973 Current Population Survey for whom IRS earnings records are available. This sample allows
4:131:10012:18:0:43:547:77:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:us to observe the earnings of CPS participants who,  for one reason or another,  failed to provide
5:132:10111:0:18:43:547:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:valid earnings information to the CPS. We show that IRS earnings predict non-response to the CPS
5:133:10207:18:18:43:547:753:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:within demographic covariate bins, with very high and very low earning individuals most likely to
5:134:10304:18:18:43:547:735:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have invalid CPS earnings records.  Measuring the degree of selection using our proposed KS metric
5:135:10402:18:18:43:547:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we find  significant  deviations from ignorability  with  patterns of  selection that vary substantially
5:136:10506:18:18:43:547:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:across demographic groups.  Given recent trends in survey imputation rates, these findings suggest
5:137:10604:18:18:43:547:681:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economists’ knowledge of the location and shape of conditional earnings distributions in the U.S.
5:138:10701:18:25:43:296:663:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may be more tentative than previously supposed.
5:139:10748:25:18:60:546:638:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The remainder of the paper is structured as follows:  Section 2 describes our index of selection
5:140:10844:18:18:43:547:620:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  our  general  approach  to  assessing  sensitivity.   Section  3  develops  our  approach  to  assessing
5:141:10953:18:18:43:547:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the sensitivity of parametric approximations to conditional quantiles.  Section 4 obtains the results
5:142:11054:18:18:43:547:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:necessary  for  estimation  and  inference  on  the  bounds  provided  by  restrictions  on  the  selection
5:143:11161:18:52:43:486:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:process.  In Section 5 we present our empirical study and briefly conclude in Section 6.
5:144:11249:52:38:43:247:514:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:2  Assessing Sensitivity
5:145:11273:38:18:43:547:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Consider  the  random  variables  (Y,X,D)  with  joint  distributionF,  whereY∈R,X∈Rland
5:146:11361:18:18:43:546:458:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:D∈{0,1}is a dummy variable that equals one ifYis observable and zero otherwise.  Denote the
5:147:11452:18:27:43:471:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution ofYgivenXand the distribution ofYgivenXandDrespectively as:
5:148:11524:27:28:116:547:413:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:Fy|x(c)≡P(Y≤c|X=x)Fy|d,x(c)≡P(Y≤c|D=d,X=x),(1)
5:149:11570:28:27:43:534:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whered∈{0,1}and further define the probability ofYbeing observed conditional onXto be:
5:150:11656:27:35:229:547:358:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:p(x)≡P(D= 1|X=x).(2)
5:151:11676:35:18:60:546:323:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In  conducting  a  sensitivity  analysis  the  researcher  seeks  to  assess  how  the  identified  features
5:152:11784:18:18:43:547:305:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ofFy|x(c) depend upon alternative assumptions regarding the process generatingD.  In particular,
5:153:11880:18:18:43:547:287:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we will concern ourselves with the sensitivity of conclusions regardingq(τ|X), the conditionalτ-
5:154:11976:18:18:43:547:269:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quantile ofYgivenX, which is often of more direct interest than the distribution function itself.
5:155:12073:18:25:43:491:251:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Towards this end, we impose the following assumptions on the data generating process:
5:156:12158:25:18:43:546:226:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f11:F:Assumption 2.1.(i)X∈Rlhas finite supportX; (ii)Fy|d,x(c)is continuous and strictly increas-
5:157:12249:18:33:43:532:208:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:ing at allcsuch that0< Fy|d,x(c)<1; (iii)Dequals one ifYis observable and zero otherwise.
5:158:12338:33:18:60:546:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  discrete  support  requirement  in  Assumption  2.1(i)  simplifies  inference  as  it  obviates  the
5:159:12443:18:18:43:547:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:need to employ nonparametric estimators of conditional quantiles.  While this assumption may be
5:160:12538:18:18:43:547:139:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:restrictive in some environments, it is still widely applicable as illustrated in our study of quantile
5:161:12641:18:18:43:547:121:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specific returns to education in Section 5.  It is also important to emphasize that Assumption 2.1(i)
5:162:12742:18:18:43:547:103:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is not necessary for our identification results, but only for our discussion of inference.  Assumption
5:163:12844:18:26:43:547:85:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2.1(ii) ensures that for any 0< τ <1, theτ-conditional quantile ofYgivenXis uniquely defined.
5:164:12937:26:0:60:546:59:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Most previous work on sensitivity analysis (e.g.  Rosenbaum and Rubin (1983),  Altonji et al.
6:165:13031:0:18:43:547:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2005)) has relied upon parametric models of selection.  While potentially appropriate in cases where
6:166:13132:18:18:43:547:753:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:particular deviations from ignorability are of interest, such approaches risk understating sensitivity
6:167:13234:18:18:43:547:735:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by  implicitly  ruling  out  a  wide  class  of  selection  mechanisms.   We  now  develop  an  alternative
6:168:13341:18:18:43:547:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:approach designed to allow an assessment of sensitivity to arbitrary deviations from ignorability
6:169:13438:18:18:43:547:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that  retains  much  of  the  parsimony  of  parametric  methods.   Specifically,  we  propose  studying  a
6:170:13545:18:18:43:547:681:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nonparametric class of selection models indexed by a scalar measure of the deviations from MAR
6:171:13639:18:18:43:547:663:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they generate.  A sensitivity analysis may then be conducted by considering the conclusions that
6:172:13735:18:17:43:547:645:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can be drawn under alternative levels of the selection index, with particular attention devoted to
6:173:13833:17:18:43:547:628:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:determination of the threshold level of selection necessary to undermine conclusions obtained under
6:174:13932:18:26:43:104:610:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ignorability.
6:175:13945:26:18:60:546:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Since ignorability occurs whenFy|1,xequalsFy|0,x, it is natural to measure deviations from MAR
6:176:14039:18:18:43:547:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  terms  of  the  distance  between  these  two  distributions.   We  propose  as  an  index  of  selection
6:177:14148:18:18:43:546:548:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the maximal Kolmogorov-Smirnov (KS) distance betweenFy|1,xandFy|0,xacross all values of the
6:178:14239:18:27:43:420:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:covariates.2Thus, forXthe support ofX, we define the selection metric:
6:179:14309:27:10:199:260:503:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:A:S(F)≡sup
6:180:14317:10:0:242:258:493:8:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f10:?:x∈X
6:181:14320:0:10:261:279:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:?:sup
6:182:14323:10:0:262:278:493:8:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f12:?:c∈R
6:183:14326:0:31:281:547:503:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:A:|Fy|1,x(c)−Fy|0,x(c)|.(3)
6:184:14351:31:18:43:547:472:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Note  that  the  missing  at  random  assumption  may  be  equivalently  stated  asS(F)  =  0,  while
6:185:14452:18:18:43:547:454:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:S(F) = 1 corresponds to severe forms of selection whereFy|1,xandFy|0,xfail to overlap at some
6:186:14545:18:18:43:547:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pointx∈ X.  For illustrative purposes,  Appendix A provides a numerical example mapping the
6:187:14636:18:18:43:547:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parameters of a bivariate normal selection model into values ofS(F) and plots of the corresponding
6:188:14734:18:26:43:215:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:observed and missing data CDFs.
6:189:14765:26:18:60:547:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Restrictions onS(F) can be shown to yield sharp tractable bounds on the conditional distribu-
6:190:14858:18:18:43:547:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion functionFy|x(·) as well as its value at any particular point of evaluationFy|x(c).  This facilitates
6:191:14963:18:17:43:546:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the study of both conditional quantiles (F−1y|x(c)) and conditional quantile processes (F−1y|x(·)) in fam-
6:192:15069:17:18:43:547:321:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ilies of non-ignorable selection mechanisms indexed byS(F).  By construction, any scalar metric of
6:193:15167:18:18:43:547:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:selection will be less informative than a full description of the selection process.  Researchers who
6:194:15268:18:18:43:547:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:suspect particular forms of heterogeneity in the selection mechanism across covariate values may
6:195:15364:18:18:43:547:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wish to consider separate indices of selection for each point in the support ofXor consider a max-
6:196:15462:18:18:43:547:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:imum of weighted KS distances in (3).  Likewise, if one has in mind particular classes of selection
6:197:15561:18:18:43:547:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mechanisms, it is possible to consider indices based upon weighted KS distances with weights that
6:198:15658:18:18:43:546:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vary across points of evaluationc.  Though such approaches entail a simple extension of our meth-
6:199:15755:18:18:43:547:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ods, we do not pursue them here.  Our approach is tailored to environments where prior knowledge
6:200:15851:18:18:43:547:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the selection mechanism is not available.  If substantial prior information is available, or if par-
6:201:15954:18:18:43:547:159:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ticular sorts of violations of MAR are of interest, it may be better to work with a semi-parametric
6:202:16053:18:25:43:238:141:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or even parametric model of selection.
6:203:16091:25:18:60:546:116:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We note in passing that parametric models of selection often imply stronger restrictions on the
6:204:16186:18:18:43:547:98:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relationship between the observed and missing data distributions than is sometimes appreciated.
6:205:16281:18:0:56:547:80:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:2The Kolmogorov-Smirnov distance between two distributionsH1(·) andH2(·) is defined as supc∈R|H1(c)−H2(c)|.
7:206:16389:0:18:43:547:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For example, the bivariate normal selection model considered in Appendix A tends to achieve maxi-
7:207:16486:18:18:43:547:753:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mal distances between missing and observed distributions at points near the center of the unselected
7:208:16586:18:18:43:547:735:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution while points in the tails of the distribution exhibit relatively small discrepancies.  How-
7:209:16690:18:18:43:547:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ever, this model cannot accommodate patterns of selection that would lead the CDFs of missing
7:210:16783:18:18:43:547:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and observed outcomes to cross at some values as might occur if individuals with very high or very
7:211:16881:18:18:43:547:681:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:low values ofYare most likely to have missing observations – a pattern conjectured to be present
7:212:16977:18:18:43:547:663:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in earnings data by Lillard et al. (1986) and corroborated in our later analysis of earnings validation
7:213:17080:18:17:43:546:645:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:data in Section 5.3In cases where crossing occurs, the maximal distance between distributions will
7:214:17178:17:18:43:547:628:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tend to be achieved far from the crossing point,  often in the tails of the unselected distribution.
7:215:17278:18:18:43:547:610:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Since one typically does not know whether or where the CDFs cross, or how this behavior varies
7:216:17372:18:18:43:547:592:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:across covariate bins, it can be difficult to develop a model of non-response suitable for the study
7:217:17472:18:18:43:547:574:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of conditional distributions.  For this reason, the consideration of a nonparametric measure of devi-
7:218:17573:18:18:43:547:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ations from MAR of the sort indexed by our maximal KS metricS(F), is likely to be of interest in
7:219:17669:18:26:43:277:538:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:most settings where missing data are present.
7:220:17714:26:18:60:546:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Forq(τ|X) the conditionalτ-quantile ofYgivenX, we examine what can be learned about the
7:221:17801:18:27:43:379:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditional quantile functionq(τ|·) under the nominal restriction:
7:222:17867:27:28:267:547:467:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:A:S(F)≤k .(4)
7:223:17878:28:18:43:547:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Knowledge of a true value ofkfor which (4) holds is not presumed.  Rather, we propose examining
7:224:17973:18:17:43:547:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the conclusions that may be drawn on the CQF given various candidate values ofk.  By consid-
7:225:18065:17:18:43:546:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ering multiple values ofk, it is possible to deduce what level of selection is necessary to overturn
7:226:18165:18:26:43:326:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conclusions of interest obtained under a MAR analysis.
7:227:18219:26:18:60:546:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the absence of additional restrictions, the conditional quantile function ceases to be identified
7:228:18319:18:18:43:547:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:under any deviation from ignorability (k >0).  Nonetheless,q(τ|·) may still be shown to lie within

7:230:18518:18:18:43:546:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution of observables were the putative restrictionS(F)≤kknown to hold.  We qualify such
7:231:18612:18:25:43:456:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a set as nominal due to restriction (4) being part of a hypothetical exercise only.
7:232:18695:25:28:60:496:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The following Lemma provides a sharp characterization of the nominal identified set:
7:233:18779:28:18:43:547:235:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f11:F:Lemma 2.1.Suppose  Assumptions  2.1(ii)-(iii)  hold,S(F)≤kand  letF−y|1,x(c)  =F−1y|1,x(c)if

7:246:19240:18:0:56:504:67:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:A:3Crossing of CDFs may also occur in two-sided selection models of the sort considered by Neal (2004).

8:254:20001:46:34:43:147:617:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.1  Examples
8:255:20014:34:17:43:547:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We conclude this section by illustrating through examples how the bound functions (qL,qU) may
8:256:20107:17:18:43:547:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be used to evaluate the sensitivity of conclusions obtained under MAR. For simplicity, we letXbe

8:258:20281:28:18:43:547:520:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Example 2.1. (Pointwise Conclusions)Suppose interest centers on whetherq(τ|X= 1) equals

8:261:20576:17:18:43:547:467:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:functions (qL(τ0|·),qU(τ0|·)).  Concretely, the minimal amount of selection necessary to overturn the
8:262:20677:18:28:43:343:449:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conclusion that the conditional quantiles differ is given by:
8:263:20738:28:27:64:547:421:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:k0≡infk:qL(τ0,k|X= 1)−qU(τ0,k|X= 0)≤0≤qU(τ0,k|X= 1)−qL(τ0,k|X= 0).(5)
8:264:20807:27:18:43:547:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:That is,k0is the minimal level of selection under which the nominal identified sets forq(τ0|X= 0)
8:265:20904:18:28:43:257:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:andq(τ0|X= 1) contain a common value.
8:266:20941:28:18:43:546:348:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Example 2.2. (Distributional Conclusions)A  researcher  is  interested  in  whether  the  con-
8:267:21035:18:17:43:547:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ditional  distributionFy|x=0first  order  stochastically  dominatesFy|x=1,  or  equivalently,  whether
8:268:21137:17:18:43:546:313:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:q(τ|X= 1)≤q(τ|X= 0) for allτ∈(0,1).  She finds under MAR thatq(τ|X= 1)> q(τ|X= 0)
8:269:21218:18:18:43:546:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at multiple values ofτleading her to conclude that first order stochastic dominance does not hold.
8:270:21316:18:18:43:547:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Employing the functions (qL,qU), she may assess what degree of selection is necessary to cast doubt

8:273:21502:27:18:43:547:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Here,k0is the smallest level of selection for which an element of the identified set forq(·|X= 1)
8:274:21599:18:18:43:547:186:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(qL(·,k0|X= 1)) is everywhere below an element of the identified set forq(·|X= 0) (qU(·,k0|X=
8:275:21692:18:18:43:547:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:0)).  Thus,k0is the threshold level of selection under whichFy|x=0may first order stochastically
8:276:21788:18:27:43:128:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dominateFy|x=1.
8:277:21803:27:18:43:547:123:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Example 2.3. (Breakdown Analysis)A more nuanced sensitivity analysis might examine what
8:278:21890:18:18:43:546:105:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:degree of selection is necessary to undermine the conclusion thatq(τ|X= 1)6=q(τ|X= 0) at each
8:279:21983:18:28:43:546:87:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specific quantileτ.  As in Example 2.1, we can define the quantile specific critical level of selection:
8:280:22087:28:0:64:547:59:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:κ0(τ)≡infk:qL(τ,k|X= 1)−qU(τ,k|X= 0)≤0≤qU(τ,k|X= 1)−qL(τ,k|X= 0).(7)
9:281:22156:0:18:43:547:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:By  consideringκ0(τ)  at  different  values  ofτ,  we  implicitly  define  a  “breakdown”  functionκ0(·)
9:282:22260:18:53:43:509:753:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which reveals the differential sensitivity of the initial conjecture at each quantileτ∈(0,1).
9:283:22353:53:37:43:252:700:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:3  Parametric Modeling
9:284:22375:37:18:43:547:663:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Analysis of the conditionalτ-quantile functionq(τ|·) and its corresponding nominal identified set
9:285:22472:18:18:43:547:645:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:C(τ,k) can be cumbersome when many covariates are present as the resulting bounds will be of
9:286:22564:18:18:43:547:627:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high dimension and difficult to visualize.  Moreover, it can be arduous even to state the features
9:287:22662:18:18:43:547:609:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of a high dimensional CQF one wishes to examine for sensitivity.  It is convenient in such cases to
9:288:22761:18:18:43:547:591:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be able to summarizeq(τ|·) using a parametric model.  Failure to acknowledge, however, that the
9:289:22856:18:26:43:422:573:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model is simply an approximation can easily yield misleading conclusions.
9:290:22929:26:18:60:547:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 1 illustrates a case where the nominal identified setC(τ,k) possesses an erratic (though
9:291:23024:18:18:43:547:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:perhaps not unusual) shape.  The set of linear CQFs obeying the bounds provide a poor description
9:292:23121:18:17:43:547:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of this set, covering only a small fraction of its area.  Were the true CQF known to be linear this
9:293:23220:17:18:43:547:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reduction in the size of the identified set would be welcome, the benign result of imposing additional
9:294:23322:18:18:43:547:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:identifying information.  But in the absence of true prior information these reductions in the size of
9:295:23424:18:26:43:535:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the identified set are unwarranted – a phenomenon we term “identification by misspecification”.
9:296:23519:26:18:60:546:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The specter of misspecification leaves the applied researcher with a difficult choice.  One can
9:297:23614:18:18:43:547:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:either conduct a fully nonparametric analysis of the nominal identified set, which may be difficult
9:298:23713:18:18:43:547:396:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to interpret with many covariates, or work with a parametric set likely to overstate what is known
9:299:23811:18:18:43:547:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:about  the  CQF.  Under  identification,  this  tension  is  typically  resolved  by  estimating  parametric
9:300:23919:18:18:43:547:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models that possess an interpretation as best approximations to the true CQF and adjusting the
9:301:24013:18:18:43:547:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corresponding  inferential  methods  accordingly  as  advocated  in  Chamberlain  (1994)  and  Angrist
9:302:24115:18:17:43:547:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (2006).  Following Horowitz and Manski (2006), Stoye (2007), and Ponomareva and Tamer
9:303:24207:17:18:43:547:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2009), we extend this approach and develop methods for conducting inference on potentially mis-
9:304:24303:18:26:43:330:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specified parametric models under partial identification.
9:305:24360:26:18:60:546:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We  focus  on  linear  parametric  models  and  approximations  that  minimize  a  known  quadratic
9:306:24459:18:18:43:547:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:loss function.  ForSa known measure onXandES[g(X)] denoting the expectation ofg(X) when

11:361:28295:0:33:43:147:771:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.1  Examples
11:362:28308:33:18:43:547:738:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  now  revisit  Examples  2.1-2.3  from  Section  2.1  in  order  to  illustrate  how  to  characterize  the
11:363:28418:18:18:43:547:720:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sensitivity  of  conclusions  drawn  under  MAR  with  parametric  models.   We  keep  the  simplifying
11:364:28521:18:28:43:530:702:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assumption thatXis scalar, but no longer assume it is binary and instead consider the model:
11:365:28613:28:27:230:547:674:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:q(τ|X) =α(τ) +Xβ(τ).(13)
11:366:28637:27:18:43:547:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Note that whenXis binary equation (13) provides a non-parametric model of the CQF, in which
11:367:28728:18:26:43:317:629:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:case our discussion coincides with that of Section 2.1.
11:368:28783:26:18:43:547:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Example 2.1 (cont.)Suppose that an analysis under MAR revealsβ(τ0)6= 0 at a specific quantile
11:369:28876:18:18:43:547:585:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:τ0.  Employing the functions (πL,πU) we may then define the critical level of selectionk0necessary
11:370:28974:18:27:43:225:567:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to cast doubt on this conclusion as:
11:371:29010:27:28:199:547:540:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:k0≡infk:πL(τ0,k)≤0≤πU(τ0,k).(14)
11:372:29042:28:25:43:525:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:That is, under any level of selectionk≥k0it is no longer possible to conclude thatβ(τ0)6= 0.
11:373:29134:25:18:43:547:487:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Example 2.2 (cont.)In a parametric analogue of first order stochastic dominance ofFy|xover
11:374:29224:18:18:43:547:469:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:Fy|x′forx < x′, a researcher examines whetherβ(τ)≤0 for allτ∈(0,1).  Suppose that a MAR
11:375:29311:18:18:43:547:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analysis reveals thatβ(τ)>0 for multiple values ofτ.  The functions (πL,πU) enable her to assess
11:376:29407:18:28:43:464:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:what degree of selection is necessary to undermine her conclusions by considering:
11:377:29489:28:27:184:547:405:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:k0≡infk:πL(τ,k)≤0    for allτ∈(0,1).(15)
11:378:29529:27:18:43:547:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Note that findingπL(τ,k0)≤0 for allτ∈(0,1) does in  fact  cast doubt on the conclusion that
11:379:29620:18:18:43:547:360:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:β(τ)>0 for someτbecauseπL(·,k0) is itself in the nominal identified set forβ(·).  That is, under
11:380:29716:18:26:43:353:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a degree of selectionk0, theprocessβ(·) may equalπL(·,k0).
11:381:29774:26:17:43:547:316:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Example 2.3 (cont.)Generalizing  the  considerations  of  Example  2.1,  we  can  examine  what
11:382:29869:17:18:43:547:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:degree of selection is necessary to undermine the conclusion thatβ(τ)6= 0 at each specificτ.  In
11:383:29965:18:28:43:386:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this manner, we obtain a quantile specific critical level of selection:
11:384:30036:28:27:195:547:253:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:κ0(τ)≡infk:πL(τ,k)≤0≤πU(τ,k).(16)
11:385:30069:27:18:43:547:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:As in Section 2.1, the resulting “breakdown” functionκ0(·) enables us to characterize the differential
11:386:30171:18:53:43:418:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sensitivity of the entire conditional distribution to deviations from MAR.
11:387:30245:53:38:43:286:155:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:4  Estimation and Inference
11:388:30272:38:18:43:547:117:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In what follows we develop methods for conducting sensitivity analysis using sample estimates of
11:389:30368:18:18:43:546:99:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:πL(τ,k) andπU(τ,k).  This section is primarily technical and applied readers may wish to skip to
11:390:30464:18:0:43:394:81:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the application in Section 5 before studying these methods in detail.
12:391:30535:0:18:60:547:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our strategy for estimating the boundsπL(τ,k) andπU(τ,k) consists of first obtaining estimates
12:392:30629:18:18:44:547:753:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ˆqL(τ,k|x) and  ˆqU(τ,k|x) of the conditional quantile bounds and then employing them in place of
12:393:30726:18:18:43:546:735:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:qL(τ,k|x)  andqU(τ,k|x)  in  the  linear  programming  problems  given  in  (10)  and  (11).   Thus,  an
12:394:30830:18:18:43:547:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:appealing characteristic of our estimator is the reliability and low computational cost involved in
12:395:30929:18:18:43:547:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:solving  a  linear  programming  problem  –  considerations  which  become  particularly  salient  when
12:396:31032:18:25:43:300:681:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implementing a bootstrap procedure for inference.
12:397:31081:25:18:60:547:656:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Recall that the conditional quantile boundsqL(τ,k|x) andqU(τ,k|x) may be expressed as quan-

16:654:41215:53:37:43:379:416:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:5  Evaluating the U.S. Wage Structure
16:655:41252:37:18:43:547:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We turn now to an empirical assessment of the sensitivity of observed patterns in the U.S. wage
16:656:41347:18:18:43:547:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:structure to deviations from the MAR assumption.  A large literature reviewed by (among others)
16:657:41442:18:18:43:547:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Autor and Katz (1999),  Heckman et al. (2006) and Acemoglu and Autor (2010) finds important
16:658:41533:18:26:43:518:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:changes over time in the conditional distribution of earnings with respect to schooling levels.
16:659:41628:26:17:60:546:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We begin our investigation of the sensitivity of these findings to alternative missing data assump-
16:660:41727:17:18:43:547:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions by revisiting the results of Angrist et al. (2006) regarding changes across Decennial Censuses
16:661:41827:18:18:43:547:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the quantile specific returns to schooling.  We analyze the 1980, 1990, and 2000 Census samples
16:662:41925:18:18:43:547:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:considered  in  their  study  but,  to  simplify  our  estimation  routine,  and  to  correct  small  mistakes
16:663:42035:18:18:43:547:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:found in the IPUMS files since the time their extract was created, we use new extracts of the 1%
16:664:42131:18:18:43:547:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unweighted IPUMS files for each decade rather than their original mix of weighted and unweighted
16:665:42227:18:26:43:547:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:samples.7Sample sizes and imputation rates for the weekly earnings variable are given in Table 1.
16:666:42324:26:27:60:497:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We estimate linear conditional quantile models for log earnings per week of the form:
16:667:42409:27:19:218:547:139:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:q(τ|X,E) =X′γ(τ) +Eβ(τ),(40)
16:668:42437:19:15:56:547:120:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:7The sample consists of native born black and white men ages 40-49 with six or more years of schooling who
16:669:42543:15:12:43:547:105:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:worked  at  least  one  week  in  the  past  year.   Rather  than  dropping  observations  with  allocated  earnings  we  treat
16:670:42670:12:12:43:547:93:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:them as missing.  We also drop 10 observations falling in demographic cells with greater than 66% missing and 1,404
16:671:42785:12:12:43:547:81:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:observations falling into demographic cells with less than 20 observations.  Use of the original extracts analyzed in
16:672:42902:12:0:43:265:69:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:Angrist et al. (2006) yields nearly identical results.
17:673:42958:0:18:43:546:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f7:B:whereXconsists of an intercept, a black dummy, and a quadratic in potential experience, andE
17:674:43050:18:18:43:547:753:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:represents years of schooling.  Our analysis focuses on the quantile specific “returns” to a year of
17:675:43150:18:18:43:547:735:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:schoolingβ(τ) though we note that, particularly in the context of quantile regressions, the Mincerian
17:676:43251:18:18:43:547:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:earnings coefficients need not map into any proper economic concept of individual returns (Heckman
17:677:43349:18:25:43:113:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (2006)).
17:678:43364:25:18:60:547:674:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 3 provides estimates of the pseudo-true returns functionsβ(·) in 1980, 1990, and 2000
17:679:43456:18:18:43:547:656:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that result from assuming the data are missing at random.  Uniform confidence regions for these
17:680:43551:18:18:43:547:638:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimates  were  constructed  by  applying  the  methods  of  Section  3  subject  to  the  restriction  that
17:681:43660:18:18:43:546:620:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:S(F) = 0.8In defining our parametric approximation metric we weight bin-specific deviations by
17:682:43754:18:26:43:413:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sample size (i.e.  we chooseSequal to empirical measure, see Section 3).
17:683:43826:26:18:60:546:576:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our MAR results are similar to those found in Figure 2A of Angrist et al. (2006).  They suggest
17:684:43921:18:18:43:547:558:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the returns function increased uniformly across quantiles between 1980 and 1990 but exhibited
17:685:44019:18:18:43:547:540:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a change in slope in 2000.  The change between 1980 and 1990 is consistent with a general economy-
17:686:44117:18:17:43:547:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wide increase in the return to human capital accumulation as conjectured by Juhn et al. (1993).
17:687:44212:17:18:43:547:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:However the finding of a shape change in the quantile process between 1990 and 2000 represents
17:688:44306:18:18:43:547:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a form of heteroscedasticity in the conditional earnings distribution with respect to schooling that
17:689:44406:18:18:43:547:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:appears not to have been present in previous decades. This pattern of heteroscedasticity is consistent
17:690:44508:18:18:43:547:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with nonlinear human capital pricing models of the sort studied in Card and Lemieux (1996) and
17:691:44602:18:47:43:524:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more nuanced multi-factor views of technical change reviewed in Acemoglu and Autor (2010).
17:692:44692:47:33:43:219:386:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5.1  Sensitivity Analysis
17:693:44717:33:18:43:547:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A natural concern is the extent to which some or all of the conclusions regarding the wage structure
17:694:44817:18:18:43:547:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:drawn  under  a  missing  at  random  assumption  are  compromised  by  limitations  in  the  quality  of
17:695:44922:18:18:43:547:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Census earnings data.  As Table 1 shows, the prevalence of earnings imputations increases steadily
17:696:45020:18:18:43:547:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:across Censuses with roughly a quarter of the observations allocated by 2000.9With these levels
17:697:45115:18:18:43:547:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of missingness, the bounds on quantiles below the 25th percentile and above the 75th are not even
17:698:45212:18:26:43:363:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:finite in the absence of restrictions on the missingness process.
17:699:45277:26:17:60:546:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We begin by examining the sensitivity of conclusions regarding changes in the wage structure
17:700:45369:17:18:43:547:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:between 1990 and 2000.  Figures 4 shows the 95% uniform confidence regions for the setG(k), as
17:701:45463:18:18:43:547:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:defined in (12), that result when we allow for a small amount of selection by settingS(F)≤0.05.
17:702:45558:18:18:43:547:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Though it remains clear the returns function increased between 1980 and 1990, we cannot reject
17:703:45652:18:18:43:547:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the null hypothesis that the quantile process was unchanged from 1990 to 2000.  Moreover, there is
17:704:45750:18:18:43:547:148:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:little evidence of heterogeneity across quantiles in the returns in any of the three Census samples –
17:705:45851:18:16:56:546:130:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:8In constructing uniform confidence intervals we setωL(τ,k) =ωU(τ,k) =φ(Φ−1(τ))1/2, whereφ(·) and Φ(·) are
17:706:45957:16:12:43:547:114:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:the standard normal density and CDF . These weights are inversely proportional to the square root of the variance
17:707:46070:12:8:43:546:102:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:of the quantiles of a standard normal.  The bootstrap weights{Wi}ni=1were drawn from an exponential distribution.
17:708:46183:8:16:56:547:94:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:9It is interesting to note that only 7% of the men in our sample report working no weeks in the past year.  Hence,
17:709:46297:16:12:43:547:78:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:at least for this population, assumptions regarding the determinants of non-response appear to be more important for
17:710:46413:12:0:43:543:66:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:drawing conclusions regarding the wage structure than assumptions regarding non-participation in the labor force.
18:711:46528:0:26:43:379:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a straight line can be fit through each sample’s confidence region.
18:712:46595:26:18:60:546:745:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To further assess the robustness of our conclusions regarding changes between 1980 and 1990,
18:713:46687:18:18:43:547:727:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it is informative to find the level ofknecessary to fail to reject the hypothesis that no change in
18:714:46786:18:17:43:547:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fact occurred between these years under the supposition thatS(F)≤k.  Specifically, forπtL(τ,k)
18:715:46880:17:18:43:547:692:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:andπtU(τ,k) the lower and upper bounds on the returns coefficients in yeart, we aim to obtain a
18:716:46975:18:28:43:352:674:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:confidence interval for the values of selectionkunder which:
18:717:47035:28:27:187:547:646:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:π80U(τ,k)≥π90L(τ,k)   for allτ∈[0.2,0.8].(41)
18:718:47080:27:18:43:547:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:As in Example 2.2, we are particularly interested ink0, the smallest value ofksuch that (41) holds,
18:719:47179:18:18:43:547:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as it will hold trivially for allk≥k0.  A search for the smallest value ofksuch that the 95% uniform
18:720:47279:18:18:43:547:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:confidence intervals for these two decades overlap at all quantiles between 0.2 and 0.8 found this
18:721:47377:18:18:43:547:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“criticalk”  to  beˆk0=  0.175.   Due  to  the  independence  of  the  samples  between  1980  and  1990,
18:722:47482:18:18:43:547:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  one-sided  interval  [ˆk0,1]  provides  an  asymptotic  coverage  probability  fork0of  at  least  90%.
18:723:47590:18:18:43:547:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The lower end of this confidence interval constitutes a large deviation from MAR (see Appendix
18:724:47684:18:18:43:547:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A) indicating the evidence is quite strong that the returns process changed between 1980 and 1990.
18:725:47782:18:26:43:512:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Figure 5 plots the uniform confidence regions corresponding to the hypotheticalS(F)≤ˆk0.
18:726:47870:26:17:60:546:467:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Though  severe  selection  would  be  necessary  for  all  of  the  changes  between  1980  and  1990  to
18:727:47975:17:18:43:547:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be  spurious,  it  is  clear  that  changes  at  some  quantiles  may  be  more  robust  than  others.   It  is
18:728:48086:18:18:43:547:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interesting  then  to  conduct  a  more  detailed  analysis  by  evaluating  the  critical  level  of  selection
18:729:48198:18:18:43:547:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:necessary to undermine the conclusion that the returns increased at each quantile.  Towards this
18:730:48294:18:28:43:491:396:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:end, we generalize Example 2.3 and defineκ0(τ) to be the smallest level ofksuch that:
18:731:48379:28:27:241:547:368:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:π80U(τ,k)≥π90L(τ,k).(42)
18:732:48403:27:18:43:547:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The functionκ0(·) summarizes the level of robustness of each quantile-specific conclusion.  In this
18:733:48502:18:18:43:547:323:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:manner, the “breakdown” functionκ0(·) reveals the differential sensitivity of the entire conditional
18:734:48602:18:26:43:368:305:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution to violations of the missing at random assumption.
18:735:48665:26:18:60:547:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The point estimate forκ0(τ) is given by the value ofkwhere ˆπ80U(τ,k) intersects with ˆπ90L(τ,k)
18:736:48761:18:18:43:547:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(see  Figure  6).   To  obtain  a  confidence  interval  forκ0(τ)  that  is  uniform  inτwe  first  construct
18:737:48870:18:17:43:547:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:95% uniform two sided confidence intervals inτandkfor the 1980 upper boundπ80U(τ,k) and the
18:738:48961:17:18:43:547:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1990 lower boundπ90L(τ,k).  Given the independence of the 1980 and 1990 samples, the intersection
18:739:49058:18:18:43:547:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the true boundsπ80U(τ,k) andπ90L(τ,k) must lie between the intersection of their corresponding
18:740:49155:18:18:43:546:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:confidence regions with asymptotic probability of at least 90%.  Sinceκ0(τ) is given by the intersec-
18:741:49256:18:18:43:547:172:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion ofπ80U(τ,k) withπ90L(τ,k), a valid lower bound for the confidence region of the functionκ0(·)
18:742:49354:18:18:43:547:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is given by the intersection of the upper envelope forπ80U(τ,k) with the lower envelope forπ90L(τ,k)
18:743:49454:18:26:43:361:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and a valid upper bound is given by the converse intersection.
18:744:49516:26:18:60:546:110:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 7 illustrates the resulting estimates of the breakdown functionκ0(·) and its corresponding
18:745:49613:18:18:43:547:92:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:confidence region.  Unsurprisingly, the most robust results are those for quantiles near the center
18:746:49712:18:0:43:547:74:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  distribution  for  which  very  large  levels  of  selection  would  be  necessary  to  overturn  the
19:747:49824:0:18:43:547:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hypothesis that the returns increased.  However the curve is fairly asymmetric with the returns at
19:748:49922:18:18:43:547:753:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:low quantiles being much more sensitive to deviations from ignorability than those at the upper
19:749:50017:18:18:43:547:735:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quantiles.  Hence, changes in reporting behavior between 1980 and 1990 pose the greatest threat to
19:750:50115:18:25:43:466:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hypotheses regarding changes at the bottom quantiles of the earnings distribution.
19:751:50197:25:18:60:546:692:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To conclude our sensitivity analysis we also consider the fitted values that result from the more
19:752:50294:18:18:43:547:674:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:flexible earnings model of Lemieux (2006) which allows for quadratic effects of education on earnings
19:753:50395:18:18:43:546:656:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quantiles.10Figure 8 provides bounds on the 10th, 50th, and 90th conditional quantiles of weekly
19:754:50491:18:18:43:547:638:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:earnings  by  schooling  level  in  1980,  1990,  and  2000  using  our  baseline  hypothetical  restriction
19:755:50599:18:18:43:547:620:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:S(F)≤0.05.  Little evidence exists of a change across Censuses in the real earnings of workers at
19:756:50696:18:18:43:547:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the 10th conditional quantile.  At the conditional median, however, the returns to schooling (which
19:757:50795:18:18:43:547:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:appear roughly linear) increased substantially, leading to an increase in inequality across schooling
19:758:50896:18:18:43:547:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:categories.  Uneducated workers witnessed wage losses while skilled workers experienced wage gains,
19:759:50995:18:18:43:547:548:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:though in both cases these changes seem to have occurred entirely during the 1980s.  Finally, we
19:760:51091:18:18:43:547:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also note that, as observed by Lemieux (2006), the returns to schooling appear to have gradually
19:761:51187:18:18:43:547:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:convexified at the upper tail of the weekly earnings distribution with very well educated workers
19:762:51284:18:46:43:347:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:experiencing substantial gains relative to the less educated.
19:763:51345:46:34:43:462:448:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5.2  Estimates of the Degree of Selection in Earnings Data
19:764:51403:34:18:43:547:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Our analysis of Census data revealed that the finding of a change in the quantile specific returns to
19:765:51504:18:18:43:547:396:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:schooling process between 1990 and 2000 is easily undermined by small amounts of selection while
19:766:51600:18:18:43:547:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:changes between 1980 and 1990 (at least above the lower quantiles of the distribution) appear to
19:767:51696:18:17:43:547:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be relatively robust.  Employing a sample where validation data are present,  we now turn to an
19:768:51791:17:26:43:527:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investigation of what levels of selection, as indexed byS(F), are plausible in U.S. survey data.
19:769:51887:26:18:60:547:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In order to estimateS(F) we first derive an alternative representation of the distance between
19:770:51981:18:18:43:547:299:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:B:Fy|0,xandFy|1,xwhich illustrates its dependence on the conditional probability of the outcome being
19:771:52080:18:27:43:446:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:missing.  Towards this end, let us define the following conditional probabilities:
19:772:52162:27:21:188:547:254:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:A:pL(x,τ)≡P(D= 1|X=x,Fy|x(Y)≤τ)(43)

19:774:52230:28:18:43:547:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:By  applying  Bayes’  Rule,  it  is  then  possible  to  express  the  distance  between  the  distribution  of
19:775:52341:18:32:43:546:187:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:missing and non-missing observations at a given quantile as a function of the selection probabilities:11

19:783:52718:18:16:52:547:88:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:10The model also includes a quartic in potential experience.  Our results differ substantively from those of Lemieux
19:784:52834:16:8:43:489:72:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:both because of differences in sample selection and our focus on weekly (rather than hourly) earnings.
19:785:52936:8:0:52:275:64:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:?:11See Appendix B for a detailed derivation of (45).
20:786:52989:0:18:43:547:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ofS(F) as well.12For this reason, our efforts focus on estimating this function in a dataset with
20:787:53086:18:26:43:326:753:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information on the earnings of survey non-respondents.
20:788:53140:26:18:60:546:727:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We  work  with  an  extract  from  the  1973  March  Current  Population  Survey  (CPS)  for  which
20:789:53239:18:17:43:547:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:merged Internal Revenue Service (IRS) earnings data are available.  Our sample consists of black
20:790:53335:17:18:43:547:692:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and white men between the ages of 25 and 50 with six or more years of schooling who reported
20:791:53427:18:18:43:547:674:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:working at least one week in the past year and had valid IRS earnings.  We drop observations with
20:792:53524:18:26:43:438:656:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:annual IRS earnings less than $1,000 or equal to the IRS topcode of $50,000.
20:793:53600:26:18:60:546:630:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As  in  our  study  of  the  Decennial  Census,  we  take  the  relevant  covariates  to  be  age,  years  of
20:794:53709:18:18:43:547:612:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:schooling, and race.  However, because our CPS sample is much smaller than our Census sample,
20:795:53802:18:18:43:546:594:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:we coarsen our covariate categories and drop demographic cells with fewer than 50 observations.13
20:796:53899:18:18:43:547:576:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This yields an estimation sample of 13,598 observations distributed across 33 demographic cells.
20:797:53995:18:18:43:547:558:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Because weeks worked are only measured categorically in this CPS extract we simply take log IRS
20:798:54090:18:18:43:546:540:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:earnings as our measure ofYand use response to the March CPS annual civilian earnings question
20:799:54184:18:25:43:353:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as our measure ofD.  This yields a missingness rate of 8.4%.
20:800:54244:25:18:60:547:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We approximate the probability of non-responseP(D= 0|X=x,Fy|x(Y) =τ) with the follow-

20:802:54383:28:21:85:504:451:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:?:P(D= 0|X=x,Fy|x(Y) =τ) = Λ(b1τ+b2τ2+δx)(M1)
20:803:54426:21:20:85:504:430:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:?:P(D= 0|X=x,Fy|x(Y) =τ) = Λ(b1τ+b2τ2+γ1δxτ+γ2δxτ2+δx)(M2)
20:804:54482:20:28:85:504:410:12:g_d0_f7:12:g_d0_f3:?:P(D= 0|X=x,Fy|x(Y) =τ) = Λ(b1,xτ+b2,xτ2+δx)(M3)
20:805:54529:28:18:43:547:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where Λ(·) = exp(·)/(1 + exp(·)) is the Logistic CDF. These models differ primarily in the degree of
20:806:54629:18:18:43:547:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:demographic bin heterogeneity allowed for in the relationship between earnings and the probability
20:807:54727:18:18:43:547:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of responding to the CPS. Model M1 relies entirely on the nonlinearities in the index function Λ(·)
20:808:54826:18:18:43:547:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to capture heterogeneity across cells in the response profiles.  The model M2 allows for additional
20:809:54925:18:18:43:547:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:heterogeneity through the interaction coefficients (γ1,γ2) but restricts these interactions to be linear
20:810:55029:18:17:43:547:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the cell fixed effectδx.  Finally, M3, which is equivalent to a cell specific version of M1, places no
20:811:55134:17:26:43:430:275:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:restrictions across demographic groups on the shape of the response profile.
20:812:55210:26:18:60:546:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Maximum likelihood estimates from the three models are presented in Table 2.14A comparison
20:813:55300:18:18:43:547:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the model log likelihoods reveals that the introduction of the interaction terms (γ1,γ2) in Model
20:814:55400:18:18:43:547:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2 yields a substantial improvement in fit over the basic separable logit of Model 1 despite the in-
20:815:55499:18:18:43:547:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:significance of the resulting parameter estimates.  However, the restrictions of the linearly interacted
20:816:55603:18:18:43:547:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Model 2 cannot be rejected relative to its fully interacted generalization in Model 3 which appears
20:817:55702:18:7:52:267:159:7:g_d0_f5:7:g_d0_f14:?:12Note thatP(D= 0,Fy|x(Y)≤τ|X=x) =∫τ
20:818:55738:7:10:261:547:152:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:0P(D= 0|Fy|x(Y) =u,X=x)dubecauseFy|x(Y) is uniformly
20:819:55790:10:0:43:317:142:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:distributed  on  [0,1]  conditional  onX=x.   ThuspL(x,τ)  =
20:820:55850:0:11:323:333:150:10:g_d0_f17:7:g_d0_f14:?:∫τ
20:821:55852:11:11:327:546:139:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:0P(D=  0|Fy|x(Y)  =u,X=x)du/τ.   Likewise
20:822:55893:11:0:43:88:128:10:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f6:F:pU(x,τ) =

20:827:55975:8:12:61:547:116:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:We use five-year age categories instead of single digit ages and collapse years of schooling into four categories:
20:828:56089:12:8:43:472:104:10:g_d0_f13:10:g_d0_f6:F:<12 years of schooling, 12 years of schooling, 13-15 years of schooling, and 16+ years of schooling.
20:829:56189:8:16:52:547:96:7:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f6:F:14We use the respondent’s sample quantile in his demographic cell’s distribution ofYas an estimate ofFy|x(Y).
20:830:56298:16:12:43:547:80:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:It can be shown that sampling errors in the estimated quantiles have asymptotically negligible effects on the limiting
20:831:56416:12:0:43:217:68:10:g_d0_f6:10:g_d0_f6:F:distribution of the parameter estimates.
21:832:56458:0:26:43:178:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to be substantially overfit.
21:833:56486:26:18:60:546:745:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A  Wald  test  of  joint  significance  of  the  earned  income  terms  (b1,b2)  in  the  first  model  easily
21:834:56596:18:18:43:547:727:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rejects the null hypothesis that the data are missing at random.  Evidently, missingness follows a U-
21:835:56697:18:17:43:547:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shaped response pattern with very low and very high wage men least likely to provide valid earnings
21:836:56796:17:18:43:547:692:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information – a pattern conjectured (but not directly verified) by Lillard et al. (1986).  This pattern
21:837:56899:18:18:43:547:674:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is also found in the two more flexible logit models as illustrated in the third panel of the table which
21:838:57003:18:18:43:547:656:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:provides the average marginal effects of earnings evaluated at three quantiles of the distribution.
21:839:57102:18:18:43:546:638:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:These average effects are consistently negative atτ= 0.2 and positive atτ= 0.8.  It is important
21:840:57198:18:18:43:547:620:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to note however that Models 2 and 3 allow for substantial heterogeneity across covariate bins in
21:841:57294:18:18:43:547:602:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these marginal effects which in some cases yields response patterns that are monotonic rather than
21:842:57392:18:26:43:94:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:U-shaped.
21:843:57401:26:18:60:546:558:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:It is straightforward to estimate the distance between missing and nonmissing earnings distribu-
21:844:57497:18:18:43:547:540:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions in each demographic bin by integrating our estimates ofP(D= 0|X=x,Fy|x(Y) =τ) across
21:845:57587:18:17:43:547:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the relevant quantiles of interest.  We implement this integration numerically via one dimensional
21:846:57685:17:18:43:547:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Simpson quadrature.  The bottom panel of Table 2 shows quantiles of the distribution of resulting
21:847:57782:18:18:43:547:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cell specific KS distance estimates.  Model 1 is nearly devoid of heterogeneity in KS distances across
21:848:57884:18:18:43:547:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:demographic bins because of the additive separability implicit in the model.  Model 2 yields sub-
21:849:57981:18:18:43:547:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stantially more heterogeneity with a minimum KS distance of 0.02 and a maximum distanceS(F)
21:850:58072:18:18:43:547:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of 0.12.  Finally, Model 3, which we suspect has been overfit, yields a median KS distance of 0.11
21:851:58170:18:26:43:292:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and an enormous maximum KS distance of 0.44.
21:852:58214:26:18:60:546:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 9 provides a visual representation of our estimates from Model 2 of the underlying distance
21:853:58312:18:18:43:546:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:functions|Fy|1,x(q(τ|x))−Fy|0,x(q(τ|x))|in each of the 33 demographic bins in our sample.  The outer
21:854:58412:18:18:43:547:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:envelope of these functions corresponds to the quantile specific level of selection considered in the
21:855:58513:18:17:43:547:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:breakdown analysis of Figure 7, while the maximum point on the envelope corresponds toS(F).
21:856:58604:17:18:43:547:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Note  that  while  some  of  the  distance  functions  exhibit  an  unbroken  inverted  U  shaped  pattern
21:857:58710:18:18:43:547:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:others exhibit double or even triple arches.  The pattern of multiple arches occurs when the CDFs
21:858:58807:18:18:43:547:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are estimated to have crossed at some quantile which yields a distance of zero at that point.  A
21:859:58903:18:18:43:547:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quadratic relationship between missingness and earnings can easily yield such patterns.  Because of
21:860:59002:18:18:43:547:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the interactions in Model 2, some cells exhibit effects that are not quadratic and tend to generate
21:861:59101:18:18:43:547:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:CDFs exhibiting first order stochastic dominance.  It is interesting to note that the demographic cell
21:862:59203:18:18:43:547:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:obtaining the maximum KS distance of 0.12 corresponds to young (age 25-30), black, high school
21:863:59297:18:18:43:547:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dropouts for whom more IRS earnings are estimated to monotonically increase the probability of
21:864:59391:18:18:43:547:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:responding to the CPS earnings question.  This leads to a distribution of observed earnings which
21:865:59488:18:25:43:412:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stochastically dominates that of the corresponding unobserved earnings.
21:866:59559:25:18:60:546:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our estimates of selection in Figure 9, when compared to the breakdown function of Figure 7,
21:867:59651:18:18:43:547:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reinforce our earlier conclusion that most of the apparent changes in wage structure between 1980
21:868:59748:18:18:43:547:95:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and 1990 are robust to plausible violations of MAR but that conclusions regarding lower quantiles
21:869:59845:18:0:43:547:77:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:could be overturned by selective non-response.  Likewise, the apparent emergence of heterogeneity in
22:870:59947:0:18:43:547:771:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the returns function in 2000, may easily be justified by selection of the magnitude found in our CPS
22:871:60047:18:18:43:547:753:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sample.  Though our estimates of selection are fairly sensitive to the manner in which cell specific
22:872:60147:18:18:43:547:735:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:heterogeneity is modeled, we take the patterns in Table 2 and Figure 9 as suggestive evidence that
22:873:60245:18:18:43:547:717:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:small, but by no means negligible, deviations from missing at random are likely present in modern
22:874:60342:18:18:43:547:699:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:earnings data.  These deviations may yield complicated discrepancies between observed and missing
22:875:60439:18:18:43:547:681:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:CDFs about which it is hard to develop strong priors.  We leave it to future research to examine
22:876:60535:18:18:43:547:663:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these issues more carefully with additional validation datasets.  Given however the likely absence of
22:877:60636:18:17:43:547:645:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:such prior knowledge for most prospective studies, we expect the sensitivity techniques developed
22:878:60733:17:53:43:309:628:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in this paper to be quite useful for applied research.
22:879:60787:53:38:43:165:575:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:6  Conclusion
22:880:60800:38:18:43:547:537:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We have proposed assessing the sensitivity of estimates of conditional quantile functions with missing
22:881:60902:18:18:43:547:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:outcome data to violations of the MAR assumption by considering the minimum level of selection,
22:882:60997:18:18:43:547:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as indexed by the maximal KS distance between the distribution of missing and nonmissing out-
22:883:61090:18:18:43:547:483:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:comes across all covariate values, necessary to overturn conclusions of interest.  Inferential methods
22:884:61192:18:18:43:547:465:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:were developed that account for uncertainty in estimation of the nominal identified set and that
22:885:61288:18:17:43:547:447:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:acknowledge the potential for model misspecification.  We found in an analysis of U.S. Census data
22:886:61386:17:18:43:547:430:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the well-documented increase in the returns to schooling between 1980 and 1990 is relatively
22:887:61483:18:18:43:547:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:robust to alternative assumptions on the missing process,  but that conclusions regarding hetero-
22:888:61580:18:18:43:547:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:geneity in returns and changes in the returns function between 1990 and 2000 are very sensitive to
22:889:61678:18:26:43:189:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:departures from ignorability.
22:890:61707:26:18:60:546:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:While  we  have  focused  on  methods  for  gauging  sensitivity  to  non-response  in  cross-sectional
22:891:61810:18:18:43:547:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:datasets,  a number of interesting extensions are possible.  An obvious (and important) one is an
22:892:61907:18:18:43:547:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:adaptation  to  environments  where  missingness  arises  due  to  non-participation  in  the  labor  force
22:893:62014:18:18:43:547:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as in Heckman (1974) and Blundell et al. (2007).  Additional side restrictions may be appropriate
22:894:62111:18:17:43:547:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:here,  particularly  in  a  panel  data  setting  of  the  sort  studied  by  Johnson  et  al.  (2000)  and  Neal
22:895:62224:17:18:43:547:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2004).  Another extension is to treatment effects where, again, researchers may wish to combine
22:896:62320:18:18:43:547:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:our  nominal  KS  restriction  with  additional  restrictions  of  the  sort  studied  by  Lee  (2009)  or  (if
22:897:62431:18:18:43:547:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:outcomes are discrete) those of Shaikh and Vytlacil (2005) and Bhattacharya et al. (2008).  Adding
22:898:62529:18:18:43:547:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:restrictions will shrink the nominal identified set and, in general, reduce sensitivity, but will also
22:899:62631:18:0:43:525:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:substantially complicate inference.  We leave the development of such methods to future work.
